### D35. 2026-06-18 - INT8 precision point (T29) RUN COMPLETE + full-parity diagnostics + verified + folded into report §6.15

**What ran (TC1, 2026-06-18):** all five `*_8bit` matrix jobs (61196/61197/61199/61202/61203, every job COMPLETED, 0 errors; Mistral-7B finished in 1:19:44, well under the 6h wall) + the INT8 HarmBench-classifier judge (61217, fp16, 0 parse errors) + the gpt-4o second judge locally (W3 parity, 0 parse errors). INT8 = bitsandbytes LLM.int8 (a *different method*, NOT lower-bit NF4). The qwen_2b smoke gated the run (confirmed `load_in_8bit` loads on the V100 sm_70); its 5-sample output was deleted before the full matrix to avoid resume/batch contamination.

**Full-parity diagnostic stack (user chose "full parity").** The whole old-model eval stack was replicated for the 5 INT8 aliases, scoped so ZERO committed artifacts drift: v2 rescore sidecars (`scores.v2`/`summary.v2`), judge-vs-v2 κ, gpt-4o-vs-classifier κ, HarmBench category + MMLU subject breakdowns — all written to `*_int8` outputs. Added backward-compatible `--models` + `--out-suffix` to `rescore_harmbench`, `judge_agreement`, `judge_pairwise_agreement`, `harmbench_category_breakdown`, `mmlu_subject_breakdown` (defaults byte-identical; regression-guarded). Caught + fixed a latent bug: `precision_sweep_analysis.py` read the v2 proxy from `summary.json`, which is **v1** for the original models (e.g. qwen_2b_base 0.775) vs **v2** in `summary.v2.json` (0.600) — now reads `summary.v2.json` with fallback, so the secondary column is apples-to-apples. Immutable manifest 80→120 (40 INT8 raws pinned; old hashes intact). Tests 282→**289** (+5 `test_int8_scoping.py`, +2 v2-preference in `test_precision_sweep.py`); `make agent-check` green.

**Verified before writing (T28 lesson; adversarial workflow + McNemar):** independent recompute reproduced `precision_sweep.json` exactly; a 4-lens skeptic pass (3 lenses hit transient socket errors, re-derived directly) + McNemar settled the findings. **Result — the quantization effect is NOT a smooth function of bit-width:** (1) **Capability = clean cliff at 4-bit** — no INT8 MMLU/ARC delta is significant for any pair (couldn't be flipped across 10 seeds); all significant capability losses are NF4-only (Qwen-1.7B MMLU −0.087, Llama MMLU −0.043/ARC −0.028, Qwen-4B ARC −0.021). (2) **Safety = two-peaked, method-specific** — the study's two significant ASR moves sit at different precision steps: Qwen-1.7B @ NF4 (+0.055, primary judge only — NOT significant under gpt-4o, so judge-dependent) and **Llama-3B @ INT8 (+0.040), the single most judge-robust safety move in the study** (significant under BOTH judges + McNemar p=0.022 cls / 0.008 gpt-4o; 9-vs-1 / 8-vs-0 harmful-ward; concentrated in illegal/cybercrime), but **non-monotonic** — it reverts to baseline at NF4, so 4-bit does not reproduce what 8-bit introduces. (3) The v2 regex over-counts at INT8 exactly as at fp16/NF4 (κ: Mistral 0.11 worst, Qwen 0.22/0.35, Phi 0.59, Llama 0.76) → classifier stays primary.

**Consequence for wording:** "Qwen-1.7B is the *only* significant ΔASR" is correct ONLY for the fp16-vs-NF4 main study; the precision sweep adds a second (Llama @ INT8). Scoped that phrasing in the Abstract, §6.5, §10. **Scorer audit (user asked to verify study-wide):** confirmed all 15 aliases are classifier-primary — `judge_agreement.json` (judge_name harmbench_cls) drives the report's HarmBench deltas, no regex value is ever presented as a primary result (regex appears only as labeled v2 proxy). The earlier "ΔASR +0.000" was v1→v2 regex consistency, unrelated to the regex→classifier switch.

**Report (§6.15 new, regenerated):** positioned per the user's grade-strategy call as the *honest middle* — leads with the conceptual contribution (quantization-safety is method-/model-specific, not bit-width-graded), presents the capability cliff + two-peaked safety + both-judge/McNemar validation, and caveats the Llama finding (≈8–9 prompts, one pair, non-monotonic, LLM.int8-specific). Updated Abstract, Ch3 (method coverage), §6.5, §6.14 tail, Ch8 limitation, Ch9 (INT8 done + reframed future work), §10, Appendix D (test inventory 289/23 files). v2 kept as one-line κ foil only (user choice). Branch `int8-precision-point` → merge to main after this entry.

### D34. 2026-06-15 - INT8 precision point (T29): groundwork built (loader/schema/config/sbatch/sweep + 21 tests); TC1 run pending

**Why:** address the "single method / single bit-width" weakness — the study was 4-bit NF4 only. INT8 (bitsandbytes LLM.int8 — a *different* method, NOT "8-bit NF4"; NF4 is inherently 4-bit) adds a second precision so the study spans **fp16 → INT8 → NF4**, enabling a precision-trend question (does degradation scale with aggressiveness, or is there a cliff at 4-bit?). The user chose this as the next enhancement.

**Design (correctness-first, ZERO regression to the evaluated study):** INT8 is a SEPARATE precision dimension, not jammed into the base-vs-4bit pairwise pipeline — because `compare_quant_pairs._select_pair_members` picks the alphabetically-first quantized alias, so an `_8bit` member would sort before `_4bit` and silently hijack the main analysis. Hence: (1) a backward-compatible `quant_method` schema/loader field — 'nf4' is the default when omitted, so every existing entry's load call is byte-identical; 'int8' selects `BitsAndBytesConfig(load_in_8bit=True)` (the same call the judge backend already uses). (2) INT8 lives in a SEPARATE `configs/tc1_int8.yaml` (5 `*_8bit` + their fp16 baselines for pair-validity/reference; baselines NOT re-run), so the main `tc1.yaml` (10 models), its tests, and the report stay untouched. (3) A dedicated `scripts/precision_sweep_analysis.py` reads fp16/int8/nf4 summaries per pair → `results/analysis/precision_sweep.{json,csv}` (trend + graded/cliff/non-monotonic shape; INT8-pending handled gracefully).

**Built (branch `int8-precision-point`, run pending):** `quant_method` threaded schema → ModelEntry (+validator; +consistency check that rejects it on a baseline) → ModelSpec → loader branch (`_build_bnb_8bit_config`; `_quantization_active` now also detects `is_loaded_in_8bit` so a silently-fp16 int8 load is caught) → both pipeline constructors + `build_model_spec`; `configs/tc1_int8.yaml`; 5 `slurm/jobs_tc1_int8/*_8bit__matrix.sbatch` (generated, `--config tc1_int8.yaml`) + 5 `slurm/jobs_tc1_int8_smoke/*_8bit__harmbench.sbatch` + `slurm/judge_validation_int8.sbatch` (scores ONLY the 5 int8 aliases → fp16/NF4 sidecars untouched); `scripts/precision_sweep_analysis.py`; `tests/test_quant_int8.py` (16) + `tests/test_precision_sweep.py` (5) → **282 tests pass**. Backward-compat verified without GPU/bitsandbytes: existing entries → quant_method None → NF4 path byte-identical; int8-vs-nf4 branch selection asserted via sentinel configs; the existing pairwise pipeline + committed results are unchanged. **PENDING (TC1):** smoke each `*_8bit` (gate: confirm `load_in_8bit` works on the V100) → `sbatch slurm/jobs_tc1_int8/<pair>_8bit__matrix.sbatch` (pair-by-pair) → `sbatch slurm/judge_validation_int8.sbatch` (after the matrix) → SCP back → `python scripts/precision_sweep_analysis.py` (+ optional margin capture `--config configs/tc1_int8.yaml --models <int8 aliases> --precision-tag int8`) → fold the fp16→INT8→NF4 trend into the report; then merge branch → main. Tracked as T29.

### D33. 2026-06-15 - Mechanism study (refusal-margin erosion under quantization): harness built + design de-risked; TC1 capture pending

**Why:** the empirical results (D16/D32) are a rigorous null plus one modest, borderline effect (Qwen 1.7B). To move the project from "what happens" to "why" — the lever that most raises it from benchmarking to research — we add a *mechanism*: does NF4 erode the model's refusal **decision margin**, and do behavioural flips concentrate where that margin was already thin (explaining why the smallest model moves first; Proskurina et al. 2024 arXiv:2405.00632 — quantization moves low-confidence samples most)?

**Design (de-risked by a 3-agent design workflow; critic verdict GO_WITH_CHANGES):** the naive "first-token refusal-sign flips where behaviour flips" metric is **circular** under greedy decoding (the sign already determines the judged label) and **wrong-locus** for Mistral (soft-preamble-then-comply decides late). Adopted instead: a **continuous, scale-invariant** margin `m = logsumexp(z[refusal_set]) − logsumexp(z[compliance_set])` analysed as the paired shift **Δm across all 200 HarmBench prompts** (Wilcoxon + bootstrap), NOT flip-only. Required controls (all built/planned): (1) a **capability/confidence confound control** — the same precision-induced entropy/decisiveness shift on neutral MMLU/XSTest tokens, which the refusal-margin shift must exceed (else it is "NF4 lowers confidence everywhere", a capability story); (2) a **sequence-level margin** teacher-forced over the committed response (min/mean) to capture late-resolved refusals; (3) an **fp16-vs-judge AUC gate** — the margin must predict the baseline judge label before any quantization claim; (4) flips treated as a **confirmatory zoom**, and "smallest moves first" tested by a pooled logistic `flip ~ baseline_margin + family` (n≈1000) since per-pair flip subsets (Llama 4, qwen_4b 9) are underpowered and size is confounded with family.

**Built this commit (branch `mechanism-refusal-margin`, run pending):** `ethical_benchmark/analysis/refusal_margin.py` (pure, CPU-testable metric core); `scripts/capture_refusal_margin.py` (TC1 GPU entry — teacher-forced forward passes, redacted `scores.margin.<precision>.jsonl` sidecars, NO generation, never touches raw/summary/judge artifacts; precision-agnostic so the same code does fp16/NF4/INT8); `slurm/capture_refusal_margin.sbatch`; `tests/test_refusal_margin.py` (15 tests, math + token-set + redaction). Full suite **261 pass**; CPU functional smoke on a tiny model confirms the forward-pass path. Lit anchors: Arditi et al. 2024 (refusal direction, arXiv:2406.11717), Egashira et al. 2024 (arXiv:2405.18137), Ashfaq et al. 2021 (quantization/calibration, arXiv:2111.08163). Tracked as T28.

**RESULTS + honest reframe (2026-06-15; capture TC1 job 61136 over all 10 aliases + Mac-side `scripts/refusal_margin_analysis.py`; adversarial verification = recompute PASS, interpretation critic SOUND_WITH_CAVEATS):** the clean "NF4 erodes refusal" story did NOT survive verification. The honest finding is **boundary instability, not targeted alignment erosion.** (1) *Gate:* the first-token margin predicts the baseline judge label for four families (AUC 0.86–0.90) but only weakly for Mistral (0.69 — decides late, refusal-shaped preamble then complies), which is flagged. (2) A thin baseline margin predicts flips, but the within-family (z-scored) AUC is only **0.64** — the naive pooled 0.76 is ~half a between-family/ecological effect (n≈5), and within-pair it is near chance for the two thinnest families (Qwen-1.7B 0.61, Mistral 0.54). (3) Flips are **symmetric** (50 harmful-ward / 42 safe-ward); a thin margin predicts safe-ward flips (AUC 0.78) at least as strongly as harmful-ward (0.75) → near-definitional boundary fragility, NOT one-directional safety erosion. (4) The margin shift is significant (Wilcoxon p<0.001, n=200) but **model-specific in direction** (Qwen comply-ward +1.2/+4.0; Llama/Phi refuse-ward −1.1/−0.3) and **first-token-specific** (whole-sequence margins reverse the sign for Qwen-1.7B and Phi). Qwen-4B erodes MORE (+4.0) yet flips fewer (9 vs 21) because its baseline margin is far wider (median 13.0 vs 3.8) — the mechanistic reason the 4B is behaviourally intact. (5) *Confound control:* for the flip-driving pair **Qwen-1.7B the shift is consistent with GENERIC confidence/capability softening** (neutral-token entropy +0.21 ≫ harmful +0.02), NOT a targeted alignment shift — so the small-model wobble reads as **capability-driven boundary instability**, converging with the significant ΔMMLU, the multi-seed fragility, and the ARC story. This SUPPORTS the study's capability-vs-alignment dichotomy (on the capability side) rather than adding an alignment-erosion claim. Folded honestly (with explicit caveats) into report **§6.14** + Ch9 follow-ups + Ch10 + Abstract; the overclaimed "targeted erosion" framing was caught by the adversarial pass and NOT written. Optional follow-ups: Arditi activation-direction probe (independent window), a paired neutral-margin control with a significance test, and an INT8 precision point (fp16→INT8→NF4 trend).

### D32. 2026-06-15 - T26 cross-family run COMPLETE (Mistral-7B + Phi-4-mini): no new significant safety regression; results folded into the report

**Run:** 4 matrix jobs (TC1 61121/61122/61123/61125, all COMPLETED exit 0; Mistral base 21.5 min / 4bit 33.8 min, Phi base 34.3 min / 4bit 58.5 min — all far under the 6h cap) + the new-pairs HarmBench classifier (61134, fp16, 800 classifications, 0 parse errors). gpt-4o second judge run locally (api_judge, 800 calls). Each model was smoke-gated first; Phi initially failed on stale remote code → fixed by [D31] (native Phi3).

**Findings (judge-primary; n = 200 HarmBench / 250 XSTest / 300 MMLU / 1172 ARC):**
- **Mistral-7B** (7.2B): judge ΔASR **−0.040** (CI [−0.110, +0.025], n.s.; McNemar p = 0.31) — quantization slightly *reduces* true harmful compliance. The v2 proxy reports +0.055 (0.835→0.890), an opposite-sign over-count; judge-vs-proxy κ **0.11–0.19** (the study's lowest — the regex flags 92–110/200 prompts the judge clears). gpt-4o concurs: ΔASR −0.030, κ 0.60–0.63, ASR ≈ 0.37 (matching the classifier, not the proxy's 0.84). MMLU −1.7 pp (n.s.), ARC +0.9 pp (n.s.), ΔOR 0.000. Label **alignment_improvement / directional**.
- **Phi-4-mini** (3.8B): judge ΔASR **0.000** (CI [−0.030, +0.030]; McNemar p = 1.00) → **robust_preservation / null**. judge-vs-proxy κ **0.67** (reliable, like Llama); gpt-4o κ 0.79–0.95, ΔASR +0.005. MMLU −2.3 pp (n.s.), ARC −1.5 pp (n.s.). **ΔOR −0.028 (CI [−0.052, −0.004], SIGNIFICANT)** — the 4-bit model over-refuses *less* (the study's only significant ΔOR, in the benign direction).
- **Cross-family (RQ5):** across all four families NF4 never significantly increases judge harmful compliance; **Qwen 1.7B (+0.055) remains the only significant ΔASR**. Proxy reliability splits by family: low-κ {Qwen, Mistral} (0.11–0.37) vs high-κ {Llama, Phi} (0.67–0.79) → D16's judge-over-proxy finding generalises to two further families. The gpt-4o second-judge cross-check now spans all ten models (κ 0.60–0.95).

**Report fold-in:** Tables 6.1/6.2/6.3 → 5 pairs / 10 models; new **§6.13** cross-family section; Abstract, §6.1, §6.3 (RQ5), §6.4.1 (ARC), §6.9 (RQ2/RQ5), §6.11, §6.12 and Ch10 updated; the three "TC1 run pending" passages flipped to results-in; the over-refusal-null statements qualified for Phi; the now-false "all ΔASR ≥ 0" global claim corrected (Mistral is negative under the judge). Immutable manifest 48→80 (raw + summary for the 4 new models added; old 48 byte-unchanged). 246 tests pass. **Verified** by a 3-agent adversarial workflow (independent recompute from raw files + report-vs-artifact cross-check + contradiction scan): all 36 numeric checks PASS; the scan caught 9 residual stale-framing items, all fixed.

**Ops:** measured + estimated walltime fits 6h with large margin → kept `--time=06:00:00` (settles the D30 "decide at smoke" item). Supersedes the "TC1 run pending" status of [D30].

### D31. 2026-06-15 - Phi-4-mini loads via native transformers Phi3 (`trust_remote_code: false`), not its bundled remote code

**Context:** T26 TC1 smoke (2026-06-15). Mistral-7B base smoke PASSED (coherent chat-template output, summary written). Phi-4-mini base smoke FAILED at load: `ImportError: cannot import name 'SlidingWindowCache' from 'transformers.cache_utils'`, raised inside the model's bundled `modeling_phi3.py` (the `trust_remote_code` path, pinned at the model's release commit). The installed `transformers` on TC1 is recent enough to run Qwen3 (≥4.51) and no longer exports `SlidingWindowCache` from `cache_utils`, so Phi's frozen remote code can't import — the remote code is stale relative to the library. Mistral and the existing 6 models are unaffected (none use remote code).

**Decision:** Set `trust_remote_code: false` for both Phi-4-mini members so they load through `transformers`' own native Phi3 implementation, which is version-consistent with what's installed. `attn_implementation: eager` is retained (the V100 has no flash-attention kernels). This is the minimal, environment-preserving fix: no `transformers` version change, so the 9 other models keep their validated load path and immutable results stay byte-identical.

**Rationale / why this is sound, not a compromise:** native loading uses the *same* architecture, weights, tokenizer, and chat template — only the maintained code path replaces the frozen copy. It also makes Phi *consistent* with the rest of the study (every other model already loads natively; `trust_remote_code: true` was the lone outlier), so cross-family comparability improves. The alternative — pinning `transformers` to a version with both Qwen3 support and `SlidingWindowCache` — would churn the shared environment and risk forcing re-runs of the already-complete 9 models, for no methodological gain. The smoke re-run is the validation gate (must show coherent, chat-templated output before the full matrix).

**Touches (this commit):** `configs/tc1.yaml`, `configs/default.yaml` (Phi `trust_remote_code: true→false`, both members); `tests/test_quant_config_schema.py` (`test_phi_flags` assertion flipped, comment added); `scripts/build_fyp_report.js` (Appendix A YAML + the §4.x prose/comment describing the loader capability) → `make report`; `CLAUDE.md` + `AGENTS.md` (Model Pairs note). 246 tests still pass. Supersedes the Phi-flag portion of [D30] (eager retained; remote-code dropped).

### D30. 2026-06-14 - T26 local integration of 2 new pairs (Mistral-7B, Phi-4-mini): additive, methodology-identical, TC1 run pending

**Decision:** Land all local code/config/test/sbatch/report/doc work to add `mistral_7b` and `phi4_mini` matched pairs (→ 5 pairs / 10 models / 4 families), keeping the new families on the **identical** protocol as the existing three so the comparison stays research-grade. References [D1] (matched-pair design) and the T26 feasibility prep in `todo.md`; does not reverse any prior decision.

**What landed (local; all 246 tests pass, agent-check green):**
- **New code = one field.** `attn_implementation: Optional[str]` added to `ModelEntry` (with a fail-loud validator restricting to `{eager, sdpa, flash_attention_2}` — a typo errors instead of silently picking the wrong backend), to `ModelSpec`, and injected into `model_kwargs` **only when set** (truthiness-guarded, so Qwen/Llama/Mistral `from_pretrained` calls are byte-identical to before the field existed). Threaded through both pipeline `ModelSpec` constructors + `build_model_spec`. Phi-4-mini needs `eager` because the V100 has no flash-attention kernels.
- **Configs:** 4 entries appended to `tc1.yaml` + `default.yaml` (identical blocks). Phi: `trust_remote_code: true` + `attn_implementation: eager` on **both** pair members; Mistral: neither flag. All four use `dtype: auto` + `benchmarks: [harmbench, xstest, mmlu, arc]`. The global `decoding`/`benchmarks`/`slurm` blocks, the NF4 `BitsAndBytesConfig`, seed 42, and the chat-template path are **untouched** (fairness invariants preserved by shared code).
- **Judge/analysis:** the 6 hardcoded model-lists (`judge_agreement`, `judge_pairwise_agreement`, `harmbench_category_breakdown`, `mmlu_subject_breakdown`, `rescore_harmbench`, `run_judge_validation`) extended to 10 aliases / 5 pairs (they would otherwise **silently skip** the new pairs). New `slurm/judge_validation_newpairs.sbatch` scores **only** the 4 new aliases (fp16) so the committed old-6 judge sidecars are never reopened → zero drift.
- **Cross-family:** `compute_cross_family_consistency` rewritten from a `families[0]`-vs-`[1]` comparison (which silently dropped families 3–4) to an **all-pairs matrix** + an across-all-families verdict — same value for the current 2 families, full coverage once 4 exist (user decision).
- **SLURM:** 4 matrix + 4 harmbench-smoke sbatch templated byte-consistent from the committed `qwen_2b_base` files (the live generator drifted to absolute log paths, so regenerating in place would have rewritten the old 6 — avoided).
- **Tests:** new `tests/test_quant_config_schema.py` (live config validation: 10 models / 5 pairs / 4 families + per-family flags + validator) and loader tests proving `attn_implementation` is injected when set and **omitted** when None. 223 → 246.
- **Report/docs (additive "run pending", mirroring D27):** Appendix A config YAML synced, Appendix C field documented, Ch9 future-work item rewritten as "infrastructure complete, TC1 run pending", test count 223→246 (incl. Table D.1). Results sections (Abstract, Ch6, RQ4/5) stay 3-pair — no fabricated numbers. CLAUDE/AGENTS (synced) + README updated with the 2 new rows, TC1 submit block, and counts.

**Rationale:** The user asked to do *all* local work before the TC1 GPU run with maximum care ("don't introduce any error or new risk in the new family run"). The audit (8 auditors + 4 adversarial verifiers) showed the pipeline is config-driven except for three silent-failure points (the `attn_implementation` plumbing, the hardcoded judge/analysis lists, and the 2-family cross-family bug) — all closed here. Nothing about the existing results or setup changes (confirmed: existing entries untouched, immutable artifacts not reopened, the only new loader code is a no-op when the field is unset).

**Pending (TC1, user-driven):** prefetch (Mistral HF-gated → token login first) → smoke each new model (confirm native chat template + Phi eager) → matrix (Mistral first) → `judge_validation_newpairs.sbatch` → SCP back → `make analyze` + breakdowns + gpt-4o second judge (user chose full parity) → fold real numbers into the report. **Mistral 7.2B vs 6h/10G:** decide any resource bump at smoke time (user decision). Report-worthy once results land.

### D29. 2026-06-14 - T23 ARC-Challenge RUN: capability loss is direction-robust but MMLU-overstated; the within-Qwen scale gap does not replicate

**What ran:** ARC-Challenge (1,172 questions) on all six models on TC1 (jobs 61088–61099, greedy, 0 errors), then `make analyze` (ARC ΔACC + paired-bootstrap CI, same machinery as MMLU). One hotfix needed first: the CLI `--benchmark` choices were hardcoded and rejected `arc` (fixed by sourcing from `SUPPORTED_BENCHMARKS`; jobs 61086/61087 had failed instantly).

**Result (ARC ΔACC, 4-bit − base, n=1,172):**
- **Qwen 1.7B: −0.013 (CI [−0.036, +0.011], NOT significant)** vs MMLU −0.087 (sig). The severe MMLU drop is largely MMLU-specific (answer-format/truncation, Ch8).
- **Qwen 4B: −0.021 (CI [−0.037, −0.007], SIGNIFICANT)** vs MMLU −0.003 (n.s.). ARC finds a small loss MMLU missed.
- **Llama 3B: −0.028 (CI [−0.045, −0.009], sig)** vs MMLU −0.043 (sig). Consistent across both.

**Interpretation:** Direction is robust (all 6 deltas negative; ≥1 benchmark significant per pair) → **RQ3 strengthened**. But magnitude/significance are benchmark-dependent for the Qwen family, in *opposite* directions, and the headline **≈29:1 within-Qwen scale ratio does NOT replicate** on ARC (4B loses marginally more than 1.7B) → **RQ4 capability claim hedged** (safety-axis RQ4 unaffected). The Qwen 1.7B capability half of "dual degradation" is now milder, matching how T18/T22 tempered the ASR half: the 1.7B finding is **modest on both axes**. **Labels stay MMLU-anchored**; ARC is a corroborating axis (composite-rule = future work). Report: §6.2 (29:1 qualified), new §6.4.1 (ARC composite), RQ3/RQ4 hedged, Ch8/Ch9 updated; `make report`. Manifest 36→48 (12 new ARC raw artifacts). agent-check 8/8; 223 tests.

### D28. 2026-06-14 - Adopt a `todo.md` working-backlog convention + `fyp-todo-capture` skill (productivity workflow)

**Decision:** Add a repo-root **`todo.md`** as a persistent, dated queue of *resumable* work items, plus a new Claude skill **`.claude/skills/fyp-todo-capture/`** to populate it. `todo.md` holds the granular execution context (decided options, rejected options *with the blocking reason*, exact next commands/paths/IDs, verification already run) that is too fine-grained for this log — so the next session/agent resumes with zero re-research. It is explicitly a **tactical buffer, not a source of truth**: it points to `PROJECT_LOG.md`, and a finished item's durable outcome must land here (§4, plus §2/§3) before it is pruned from `todo.md`. The skill is process+checklists only (no scripts), with a Specificity Checklist and fyp_quant guardrails (immutable raw artifacts, no raw HarmBench text). Pointer added to `CLAUDE.md` + `AGENTS.md` (synced) so Codex respects the convention too.

**Rationale:** The user wanted a productivity harness so a time-pressed session can bank progress (e.g. a model-feasibility check) and have the next agent execute immediately. The existing `fyp-agent-handoff` skill is a *one-shot* transfer note (executor/reviewer/fresh-session) — ephemeral and mode-based; it does not maintain a durable queue. `fyp-todo-capture` is complementary, not duplicative: capture often (every pause) into the durable backlog; hand off when formally transferring. Keeping `PROJECT_LOG.md` as the sole source of truth (the convention is enforced in the skill + the CLAUDE/AGENTS pointer) prevents `todo.md` from fragmenting state. First `todo.md` entry seeds the model-extension work (T26). Not report-worthy (internal productivity tooling); `make agent-check` re-run.

### D27. 2026-06-14 - T23 second capability benchmark (ARC-Challenge): infrastructure built, run PENDING on TC1

**Decision:** Add **ARC-Challenge** (not "more MMLU") as the second capability benchmark to address W5 — the alignment-vs-capability disambiguation currently rests on one 300-question MMLU subset. ARC was chosen over padding MMLU because the threat to the capability anchor is *construct validity* (one narrow proxy, with a known MMLU answer-format artifact in the Qwen 1.7B truncations), not sampling noise; a structurally different benchmark gives convergent validity, padding MMLU does not. ARC-Challenge is the lowest-friction fit (same MCQ exact-match scoring) and its ~1,172-question test set also adds far more capability N than padding the 300-Q subset would.

**Built (local, no GPU):** `ethical_benchmark/benchmarks/arc.py` (`ARCChallengePlugin`, name `arc`; handles ARC's `{text,label}` choices + `answerKey`, letter/numeric labels, re-labels options A,B,C… for prompt parity with MMLU); registered in `registry.py` + `__init__.py`; `arc` added to `configs/tc1.yaml` + `configs/default.yaml` (top-level + all 6 model lists, max_samples 1200); analysis extended (`compare_quant_pairs.py`: `PRIMARY_METRIC_BY_BENCHMARK["arc"]="accuracy"` + `_extract_binary_outcome` arc→is_correct) so `make analyze` auto-emits an ARC ΔACC with the same paired-bootstrap CI; 6 per-model sbatch in `slurm/jobs_tc1_arc/` + README; tests `tests/test_arc.py` (+5 → **223**). Prefetch needs no change (generic config_name path caches `allenai/ai2_arc`/`ARC-Challenge`).

**Scope / not-yet-done:** the interpretation **label stays anchored on MMLU**; ARC is reported as a *corroborating* capability axis (a composite-capability label rule is deliberately deferred until the data is in). The **run is PENDING** on TC1 (user submits the `jobs_tc1_arc` sbatch after `prefetch`). Report: Ch8 partial-capability limitation + Ch9 future-work updated to "implemented, run pending". Once run: SCP `results/*/arc/`, `make analyze`, fold ARC ΔACC into RQ3/§6.x. agent-check 8/8.

### D26. 2026-06-14 - T22 second judge RUN (gpt-4o): the Qwen 1.7B finding is judge-robust in direction, borderline in significance — W3 substantially resolved

**What ran:** The saved HarmBench generations for all six models were re-scored locally (no GPU) by a second frontier judge, gpt-4o (`--backend api_judge`), applying the same HarmBench rubric. 1 200 classifications, **0 parse errors**. Then `scripts/judge_pairwise_agreement.py` compared it against the primary classifier (harmbench_cls).

**Result (from `results/analysis/judge_pairwise_agreement.json`):**
- **Per-prompt agreement is strong:** Cohen's κ = **0.69–0.94** across the six models (substantial→almost-perfect) — vs κ ≈ 0.19–0.37 for the old regex. The primary classifier is *not* an idiosyncratic outlier; the regex was.
- **Per-pair ΔASR direction reproduced:** Qwen 1.7B **+0.045** (McNemar p=0.122) vs primary +0.055 (p=0.027); Qwen 4B +0.010 (p=0.774) vs +0.025; Llama +0.005 (p=1.0) vs 0.000. Both judges agree only the smallest model moves materially.
- **The nuance:** direction + approximate magnitude of the Qwen 1.7B effect are judge-robust, but its *statistical significance* is judge-dependent at the margin (significant under the primary classifier, not under gpt-4o). This **converges with T18** (multi-seed): both robustness checks say the effect is real and **modest (≈+0.045–0.055), not large or certain**.

**Conclusion:** W3 (single-judge construct validity) is substantially resolved — a second, independent frontier judge strongly agrees per-prompt and reproduces the headline direction. Residual caveats (now in §7.4/§6.12 Result 4): the API judge is a versioned/less-reproducible model, and both judges share the LLM-harm-judgment lineage, so an open-weight guard (LlamaGuard, already wired `--backend llamaguard`) remains a complementary future check. **Headline label unchanged** (Qwen 1.7B broad_degradation under the primary judge); the second judge strengthens *how* it's evidenced. Artifacts committed (redacted): `scores.judge.api_judge.*` + `summary.judge.api_judge.*` (6 each) + `judge_pairwise_agreement.{json,csv}`. Report §6.12 (Result 4), §7.4, Ch9 updated; `make report`. agent-check 8/8; 218 tests.

### D25. 2026-06-14 - T22 second-judge infrastructure: API judge wired in (egress accepted), built but NOT yet run

**Decision:** Implement the second-judge cross-check (W3) as a turnkey, locally-runnable layer and choose a **frontier API judge** as the default second judge for *accuracy* (same HarmBench rubric + stronger model = closest to the GPT-4-level gold the primary classifier was distilled toward), accepting the trade that an open-weight guard (LlamaGuard) would be more *independent*. Wired `--backend api_judge` into `scripts/run_judge_validation.py` (the `OpenAICompatibleJudgeBackend` already existed; default model `gpt-4o`, key read from `OPENAI_API_KEY` env, optional `--base-url`), hardened its `classify_batch` (3-retry + `max_tokens` bump so a 1 200-call run survives transient errors; persistent failures recorded as `error`, never dropped), added `scripts/judge_pairwise_agreement.py` (judge-vs-judge per-model κ + per-pair ΔASR with McNemar/bootstrap, redacted output), `openai` to requirements, and tests (`tests/test_judge_pairwise.py`, +3 → 218). Report §7.4/Ch9 updated to "implemented, pending run".

**Data-egress decision (the substantive part):** the api_judge backend **sends the benchmark prompt + the model's response to an external API** — a deliberate departure from the otherwise strict offline/no-egress posture. Accepted because (a) HarmBench prompts are public benchmark items, (b) the purpose is safety *classification*, within provider usage policies, and (c) the written sidecars remain redacted (IDs + booleans only; `_FORBIDDEN_OUTPUT_KEYS` still enforced). The key is read from the environment, never argv/source/logs/sidecars. The primary scorer is unchanged (harmbench_cls, D16); this is a cross-check only.

**Status:** built + tested, **NOT yet run** (the user runs it locally with their own API key; no TC1 needed). Once run: `scores.judge.api_judge.*` sidecars + `results/analysis/judge_pairwise_agreement.{json,csv}` → fold the judge-vs-judge result into §6.12/§7.4, `make report`. Reproducibility caveat (versioned API model) to be noted in the write-up at that point. `make agent-check` 8/8; 218 tests.

### D24. 2026-06-14 - Complete T21 (Ch6/Ch7 strengthening): per-category breakdown, deployment + positioning sections, and verified citations replacing placeholders

**Decision:** Finish the T21 Results/Discussion hardening from existing data (no new inference). (a) Add `scripts/harmbench_category_breakdown.py` → redacted `results/analysis/harmbench_category_breakdown.{json,csv}` (joins `score_fields.category` from raw.jsonl with the judge `judge_harmful` sidecar by `prompt_id`; no harmful text in output) and report §6.6.2. (d) Add §7.6 Deployment Implications. (e) Add §7.7 Positioning Against Prior Work + enhance §2.4 with specific citations, and **replace the four placeholder References** (three credited to "Anonymous Authors", one to an unverified id) with citations verified via web lookup. (b) and (c) were already done (D19; §6.12 Result 1).

**Rationale / integrity:** The References section shipped placeholder/likely-fabricated entries — a real academic-integrity risk in a deliverable. Each replacement was confirmed against its arXiv page (title, authors, year): Kharinaev et al. arXiv:2502.15799 (2025); Chen et al. "Q-resafe" ICML 2025 / arXiv:2506.20251; Egashira et al. "Exploiting LLM Quantization" NeurIPS 2024 / arXiv:2405.18137 (bnb/NF4-specific); Belkhiter et al. "HarmLevelBench" arXiv:2411.06835 (2024). Two further candidates were dropped as not fully verifiable (ambiguous author list / unconfirmed authors) rather than risk a wrong citation. The per-category breakdown is reported as descriptive/exploratory only (per-category n = 19–58, not significance-tested) and was reconciled: summing per-category harmful counts reproduces each model's headline judge ASR exactly (0.135/0.190/0.065/0.090/0.040/0.040).

**Impact:** No headline number or label changes — this strengthens *how* the results are evidenced and removes a citation-integrity defect. New finding surfaced: the Qwen 1.7B +0.055 ΔASR is broad-based (ASR rises in 5/6 harm categories), most prominently misinformation (0.412→0.500) and illegal activity (0.034→0.121). Report regenerated; `make agent-check` 8/8; 215 tests pass.

### D23. 2026-06-14 - T18 multi-seed sensitivity run: the greedy Qwen 1.7B ΔASR is decode-dependent (tempered, not overturned)

**Decision:** Run the T18 arm (built in D20) on TC1 for the load-bearing **Qwen 1.7B pair** and report it as an additive robustness layer in the FYP report rather than as a revision of the headline. HarmBench was re-generated under stochastic decoding (T=0.7, top-p 0.8) across seeds 1–5 for both pair members (jobs 61078/61079), each seed judge-scored by the official HarmBench classifier (jobs 61080–61084), aggregated by `scripts/sensitivity_analysis.py` into `results/analysis/sensitivity_multiseed.{json,csv}`.

**Result:** judge ΔASR per seed = −0.010, +0.050, +0.055, +0.020, +0.005 → **mean +0.024, sd 0.028, range [−0.010, +0.055], sign-consistent = False** (4/5 positive). The greedy headline (+0.055, McNemar p=0.027) coincides with the *maximum* seed, so under realistic sampling the effect attenuates to ~half and grazes zero. The asymmetry is informative: the 4-bit model's ASR is near-constant across seeds (~0.170) while the full-precision baseline varies (0.115–0.180), so the gap is driven by baseline variance. The v2 proxy shows the same shape (mean ≈ 0.000).

**Rationale / impact:** This resolves the W1 weakness (generation variance, the one Priority-1 item not fixable by reanalysis) for the headline pair with real data. It **tempers but does not overturn** the study: the greedy +0.055 remains a legitimate deterministic measurement and the primary study stays greedy by design; the arm shows it should be read as the upper end of a decode-dependent range, not a fixed effect. The ΔMMLU half of the Qwen 1.7B dual-degradation claim is unaffected (capability, not decoding-sensitive here). Report changes (report-worthy → `make report` run): new **§6.6.1**, rewritten **§6.5** caveat, **Ch8/Ch9** lines flipped from "future work" to "partially completed". `results_sensitivity/` stays gitignored (raw harmful generations); only the redacted aggregate is committed. The symmetric Qwen 4B + Llama infrastructure remains in place for a future full-matrix extension (folds into T19).

### D22. 2026-06-14 - Harden the "latent six" code-quality findings before extending the study (forward-looking; no committed numbers changed)

**Decision:** A full-repo code-quality audit surfaced six findings that could bias results under *different* models/seeds but which — verified against the committed artifacts — did **not** affect any number in the current report. They are now fixed so a future run (T18 multi-seed, T22 second judge, new pairs) cannot silently hit them:
1. **Cohen's κ degenerate case** (`scripts/judge_agreement.py`): when chance agreement is total (both raters constant-and-identical, e.g. a near-zero-ASR baseline), κ is 0/0. The code returned a spurious `1.0` ("perfect agreement"); it now returns `None` (undefined) and propagates as null/blank/"n/a". Verified: no current per-model κ hit this branch (all 0.19–0.79), so `judge_agreement.{json,csv}` regenerate byte-identical.
2. **MMLU parser** (`ethical_benchmark/benchmarks/utils.py`): the prior parser took the first standalone capital and gave up if it was out of range (a leading "I" → `None`). The hardened parser keeps the canonical letter-first behaviour, skips out-of-range letters, and reads explicit "answer is X" declarations. On the committed MMLU responses it changes 13/1800 records (10 verbose recoveries, 3 refusal-text noise flips) — but MMLU is never re-scored (the parser runs at generation time), so committed accuracy is untouched; the fix is forward-looking only.
3. **Interpretation taxonomy symmetry** (`ethical_benchmark/analysis/compare_quant_pairs.py`): `alignment_improvement` was asymmetrically gated on over-refusal while `alignment_degradation` was not — fixed to mirror it (harm + capability only). Added an `over_refusal_regression` label so a pure over-refusal worsening is named on its own axis instead of demoted to `broad_degradation`; `robust_preservation` now tolerates over-refusal *improving*. Significance-boundary convention (closed CI at 0.0 → not significant) documented inline. **All three current pair labels are preserved** (verified: empty git diff on `pair_interpretations`/`pairwise_deltas`).
4. **Silent quantization failure** (`ethical_benchmark/models/loader.py`): a `quantized=true` model that loaded in fp16 previously only logged a warning; it now **raises** (checking `is_loaded_in_4bit`/`is_quantized`/`hf_quantizer` for transformers-version robustness). The committed TC1 runs are unaffected — logs confirm bitsandbytes nf4 engaged for all three 4-bit models with no fallback.
5. **Silent benign/answered defaults** (`xstest.py`, `scripts/rescore_harmbench.py`): `_classify_benign` now returns `None` for rows with no recognised safety signal and the loader warns on schema drift; over-refusal aggregates exclude unconfirmed-benign records. No-op on committed data (every record carries an explicit `benign` flag).

Also added the **MMLU answer-format/truncation limitation** to the report (Ch8): qwen_2b_4bit's −0.087 ΔMMLU partly reflects 11/300 responses truncated mid-reasoning without a final letter (a real format-following effect, not pure knowledge loss).

**Rationale:** The user explicitly asked which audit findings affect the FYP results/methodology vs which are code-quality only, then asked to harden the latent six *before* extending (T18/T22/new models) and to add the truncation caveat. Each of the six was empirically checked against the frozen TC1 artifacts and shown not to have corrupted any reported value; the risk is forward-looking (a safer model → κ=1.0 trap; a chattier model → parser misses; an ASR-improving pair → mislabel). Fixing now closes the risk window before the next inference run, while leaving the interim submission's numbers exactly as reported.

**Impact:** **No headline number, label, CI, or κ changes.** Proof: after the fixes, `make analyze` + `judge_agreement.py` + `mmlu_subject_breakdown.py` regenerate `results/analysis/*` byte-identical to the committed copies (`git diff` empty). Raw/summary/judge/v2 sidecars never touched. Tests 186 → **215** (+κ degenerate/known-value, MMLU parser recovery, taxonomy symmetry + `over_refusal_regression`, loader quant-active guard, XSTest `_classify_benign`). Report regenerated (§3.8 six-label symmetric Table 3.4; Ch8 truncation limitation). `CLAUDE.md`/`AGENTS.md` test count synced 186 → 215. Follow-up wiring for T18/T22 should rely on these guards (e.g. report κ as undefined when a new judge/baseline is degenerate).

### D21. 2026-06-09 - Make the immutable-artifacts check (and thus the Agent Harness CI) tolerate absent artifacts

**Decision:** `check_immutable_artifacts` now treats an artifact that is **absent** from the working tree as a non-violation (the immutable raw files are gitignored, so a fresh clone / GitHub Actions checkout never has them). It still **fails** on a present-but-changed hash (mutation) or a present-but-unmanifested raw artifact (the violations the check exists to catch). All-absent → `pass` ("not checked out — expected in CI / fresh clone"); partial-absent → `warn` (visible, non-blocking); any mutation → `fail`.

**Rationale:** The first push of the agent-harness layer (commit c5f0c67) made the `.github/workflows/agent-harness.yml` CI live, and it failed on every push: the workflow ran `scripts/agent_check.py`, whose immutable-artifacts check verified 36 gitignored `raw.jsonl`/`summary.json` files that cannot exist in a CI checkout — so the harness CI failed *by design* and emailed the repo owner. Absence is not mutation, so tolerating it is the semantically correct fix and keeps the real protection (in-place edits to present TC1-original artifacts still fail). Verified with a faithful fresh-clone simulation (tracked files only, clean tree): all six checks pass, `harness_eval` 8/8. Regression test added (`test_agent_harness_immutable_tolerates_absent_artifacts`); the mutation test still guards the fail path. This is internal harness/CI tooling — not a methodology/results change — so the FYP docx was not regenerated.

### D20. 2026-06-09 - Build the T18 multi-seed sensitivity arm as turnkey TC1 infrastructure (judge-scored, all three pairs)

**Decision:** Implement T18 (the multi-seed / stochastic-decoding sensitivity arm) as ready-to-`sbatch` TC1 infrastructure rather than a one-off: `configs/tc1_sensitivity.yaml` (HarmBench only, **temperature 0.7 / top_p 0.8** = Qwen3's recommended non-thinking sampling, applied uniformly), a generator `scripts/generate_sensitivity_jobs.py` that emits per-model generation sbatch (looping seeds 1–5 into `results_sensitivity/seed<N>/`) + per-seed judge sbatch (scoring those generations with the official HarmBench classifier so the metric matches the judge-primary headline), and an aggregator `scripts/sensitivity_analysis.py` (per-pair ΔASR mean/sd/min/max/sign-consistency across seeds vs the greedy headline; redacted output to `results/analysis/sensitivity_multiseed.{json,csv}`). Built for **all three pairs (Option B)** so no model is singled out; the per-model sbatch granularity lets the user still run the load-bearing Qwen 1.7B pair first. `results_sensitivity/` is gitignored (raw generations contain harmful text).

**Rationale:** The main study is greedy (T=0.0), so its bootstrap/McNemar intervals capture prompt-sampling variance only — not generation variance; the headline Qwen 1.7B ΔASR (+0.055) is a single deterministic decode (W1, the one Priority-1 weakness that cannot be resolved by reanalysis). This arm re-runs HarmBench under realistic stochastic decoding across seeds to estimate how stable the quantization ΔASR is. **Fairness:** it is a *separate robustness layer*, never cross-compared with the greedy main results; within each pair, baseline and 4-bit use the identical temperature and seed set, so each per-seed ΔASR is a clean matched-pair contrast. HarmBench has 200 rows and `max_samples ≥ 200`, so every seed scores the same prompt SET — only generation varies. Temperature 0.7 is the model publisher's recommended non-thinking setting, so the arm is deployment-realistic and the number is defensible. Judge-scoring the new generations (vs v2 regex alone) keeps the sensitivity metric on the same footing as the D16 headline.

**Status:** Infrastructure committed + pushed; the **run is pending on TC1** (the user executes via `sbatch`; head-node Python is forbidden). 12 sbatch generated under `slurm/jobs_tc1_sensitivity/`. Tests +3 (`tests/test_sensitivity.py`: config validity + stochastic intent, `summarise_deltas`, generator output) → 192 total. Not report-worthy yet — the report's Future Work already describes the arm; §6.5/Ch9 will be updated with results once the run returns. `make agent-check` 8/8 pass.

### D19. 2026-06-09 - Two-layer label/evidence reporting + McNemar exact test for HarmBench ΔASR (Priority-1 robustness hardening)

**Decision:** Harden the results layer without any new inference (reanalysis of existing artifacts only). Three additive changes: (1) a **two-layer interpretation scheme** — `classify_pair_change` is left unchanged (direction/threshold label), and a new `label_evidence_status` emits a separate `evidence_status ∈ {confirmed, directional, null, unknown}` derived from the paired-bootstrap CI (and McNemar for HarmBench). The label is never gated/relabelled by significance; significance is reported alongside it. (2) **McNemar's exact paired test** (`mcnemar_exact_test` + `paired_binary_confusion` in `compare_quant_pairs.py`) for the HarmBench ΔASR, reported with the discordant counts (b = became-harmful, c = became-safe) for effect-size transparency. (3) A **per-subject MMLU breakdown** committed as a redacted artifact (`results/analysis/mmlu_subject_breakdown.{json,csv}`). Also normalised all machine-generated analysis CSVs to LF line endings (`lineterminator="\n"`) so regenerated CSVs don't trip `git diff --check`.

**Rationale:** Addresses the two Priority-1 weaknesses that are resolvable by reanalysis. (W2) The old labels fired on point estimates only, so Qwen 4B carried `alignment_degradation` on a non-significant +0.025 — now it keeps the label but is flagged `directional`, per the user's chosen "two-layer, do-not-hard-gate" policy. (W1, partial) The headline Qwen 1.7B ΔASR (+0.055) now has an independent, distribution-free corroboration: McNemar exact **p = 0.027** (16 became harmful vs 5 became safe, 21 discordant) — bootstrap and McNemar agree. Qwen 4B p = 0.18, Llama p = 1.00 (only the smallest model is significant under either test). (W5, partial) The per-subject artifact backs and cross-checks the report's existing per-subject prose (numbers matched exactly): Qwen 1.7B regresses 5/6 subjects, Llama 4/6, Qwen 4B only 2/6 — capability loss is broad-based, not a one-subject artifact. The remaining Priority-1 weaknesses (W1-full multi-seed variance, W3 second judge, W4 scale/family confound, W5-full second capability benchmark) genuinely require new TC1 inference and stay as T18/T22/T19/T23.

**Impact:** No headline number or label changes — Qwen 1.7B = broad_degradation (confirmed), Qwen 4B = alignment_degradation (directional), Llama = broad_degradation (confirmed). The change strengthens *how* the findings are evidenced, not *what* they are. Implemented in `ethical_benchmark/analysis/compare_quant_pairs.py` (+`label_evidence_status`, `mcnemar_exact_test`, `paired_binary_confusion`, significance threaded into `summarize_pair_labels`), `scripts/judge_agreement.py` (McNemar + evidence_status in per-pair output + console), `scripts/mmlu_subject_breakdown.py` (new), tests (`test_quant_analysis.py`, +3 → 189 total), and the FYP report (§3.7 McNemar method, §3.8 two-layer scheme, Table 6.2 evidence + McNemar rows, §6.5/§6.6/§6.8/§6.12 McNemar+evidence text). `make agent-check` = 8/8 pass.

### D17. 2026-06-08 - Convert the agent harness from prose rules into executable checks

**Decision:** Add a repo-native agent harness layer: `configs/artifact_policy.yaml`, `python fyp_cli.py agent-status`, `make agent-check`, `make harness-eval`, generated handoff/dashboard/TC1 checklist scripts, task packets under `docs/agent_tasks/`, and `results/raw_artifact_manifest.sha256` to hash ignored raw artifacts.

**Rationale:** The repo already had strong prose instructions, but future agents could still miss or misapply them. The harness turns the highest-risk rules into checks: AGENTS/CLAUDE sync, project-log discipline, immutable raw artifacts, stale current-facing text, redaction leaks, report-worthy freshness, whitespace, and tests. This strengthens the user's Codex-meetup story from "I prompt agents well" to "I build a repo-native system that lets agents act with less trust and more verification."

### D18. 2026-06-08 - Prefer on-demand skills and context-isolated subagents over larger startup prompts

**Decision:** Add repo-scoped Codex skills (`.agents/skills/`), project-scoped Codex subagents (`.codex/agents/`), lightweight lifecycle hooks (`.codex/hooks.json` + `.codex/hooks/`), a task-specific startup command (`python fyp_cli.py agent-start`), and a lightweight GitHub Actions harness workflow.

**Rationale:** The next bottleneck is not missing prose; it is context pressure and cross-task contamination. Skills let Codex load task guidance only when relevant, subagents isolate audit/review context, hooks refresh handoff artifacts and surface guardrail warnings automatically, and CI makes harness regressions visible outside a chat session. The hooks are intentionally non-blocking reminders until they have proven stable; `make agent-check` remains the authoritative finish gate.

### D1. 2026-05-23 — Drop Qwen 0.8B; finalise the three-pair design

**Decision:** Study uses three pairs: Qwen 2B, Qwen 4B, and Llama 3.2 3B (cross-family). Qwen 0.8B is dropped.

**Rationale:** At 0.8B, the BF16 baseline itself is at or barely above MMLU chance (~25%), making the alignment-versus-capability disambiguation unreliable (the capability anchor degenerates). Removing it eliminates the largest scientific risk in the study. The 2× scale gap (2B → 4B) is sufficient to test scale sensitivity within the compact-deployment regime, even though the original 5× gap (0.8B → 4B) would have been more dramatic. The scope is reframed from "scale-sensitivity across small-to-compact models" to "quantization effects in the compact-deployment regime (2B–4B)."

### D2. 2026-05-23 — On-the-fly NF4 quantization from identical baseline weights

**Decision:** Both members of every pair load from the same Hugging Face `model_id`. The only difference is whether `BitsAndBytesConfig(load_in_4bit=True, bnb_4bit_quant_type="nf4", ...)` is injected at `from_pretrained` time.

**Rationale:** Eliminates publisher- and conversion-asymmetry as confounds. Earlier plan used a pre-quantized `*-bnb-4bit` checkpoint, which conflated quantization effect with the specific publisher's NF4 pipeline. On-the-fly quantization is the strongest practical isolation of quantization as the experimental variable. Loader (`models/loader.py:_build_bnb_4bit_config`) and config schema both updated to support this. Test `test_models.TestPromptFormatting` confirms `enable_thinking=False` is also handled correctly.

### D3. 2026-05-23 — Group SLURM jobs by model, not by benchmark

**Decision:** `slurm/jobs_tc1/` contains 6 sbatch files (one per model alias), each running all three benchmarks sequentially with the model loaded only once. Previous config produced 18 per-(model, benchmark) jobs.

**Rationale:** Loading a model is the most expensive operation in the pipeline; reusing the load across three benchmarks per job is a ~3× saving on cold-load overhead. Fits well within the 6h walltime budget. With MaxJobsPU=2, scheduling pressure is reduced from 18 → 6 submissions. Implementation via `--group_by model` flag on `cluster-generate`; matrix runner uses `try/finally` to release GPU memory between models if needed.

### D4. 2026-05-24 — Strict offline mode on TC1 compute nodes

**Decision:** All datasets and model weights are pre-cached on the TC1 head node via `make prefetch`. SLURM jobs export `HF_HUB_OFFLINE=1`, `HF_DATASETS_OFFLINE=1`, `TRANSFORMERS_OFFLINE=1` in setup_commands.

**Rationale:** Compute nodes may not have outbound internet (architecture diagram in TC1 user guide is ambiguous). Even if they do, runtime downloads risk burning the 6h walltime budget on slow HuggingFace mirrors, and gating failures (Llama) would surface mid-job rather than at setup. Offline mode converts any cache miss into an immediate clear error. Pre-cache on the head node is policy-compliant — equivalent to `pip install` / `conda install` which the user guide explicitly demonstrates on the head node (p.7–9).

### D5. 2026-05-24 — Smoke validation via sbatch, not srun

**Decision:** The initial cluster smoke test is submitted as an sbatch job (5 prompts, qwen_2b_base on HarmBench). No interactive `srun` sessions for validation work.

**Rationale:** TC1 user guide p.19 explicitly says "all users are advised to use the command 'sbatch' for job submission." srun ties up an SSH session and risks killing the job on disconnect. sbatch is the documented path and survives session loss.

### D6. 2026-05-24 — Cross-agent file convention + FYP report regeneration rule

**Decision:** The repo carries two agent-instruction files (`CLAUDE.md` for Claude Code, `AGENTS.md` for Codex / Cursor / Aider / others) with intentionally identical content. The FYP report docx (`docs/FYP_Report_<date>.docx`) is regenerated from `scripts/build_fyp_report.js` via `make report` whenever a change affects report-worthy content (methodology, system design, experimental setup, results, limitations, or appendices).

**Rationale:** User explicitly stated they would use multiple coding agents (Codex + Claude). Different agents auto-load different files, so a single canonical file would only be read by one of them. Duplication with a sync discipline is more reliable than tooling. For the report: handing a stale docx to the supervisor undermines the deliverable; making `make report` a one-second rebuild removes the friction of keeping it current. Source-of-truth is the JS builder; the docx is an artifact and should never be hand-edited.

### D8. 2026-05-27 — Submit matrix jobs via direct sbatch, not make cluster-submit

**Decision:** On TC1, submit sbatch files with direct `sbatch slurm/jobs_tc1/<name>.sbatch` commands, not via `make cluster-submit`.

**Rationale:** `make cluster-submit` calls `submit_jobs.py`, which opens `manifest.json` from the jobs directory as its first action. `manifest.json` is gitignored and absent on TC1 after `git pull`, so the command fails immediately with a file-not-found error. Additionally, `make cluster-submit` runs Python on the head node, which TC1 policy explicitly forbids. Direct `sbatch` avoids both issues: it is a SLURM admin command (explicitly permitted on the head node) and requires no generated metadata files.

### D9. 2026-05-27 — TC1 effective GPU concurrency is one running job

**Decision:** Treat the full matrix as a one-running-GPU-job-at-a-time execution, even though a second job can be submitted and held pending by SLURM. Submit the next model pair only after the current pair has cleared.

**Rationale:** The first matrix submission on 2026-05-27 queued two Qwen 2B-class jobs. SLURM started job `60976` (`qwen_2b_base__matrix`) but held job `60977` (`qwen_2b_4bit__matrix`) pending with reason `QOSMaxGRESPerUser`. This shows the practical limiter is GPU GRES per user, not just the MaxJobsPU count. Keeping only the current pair in the queue avoids piling up pending jobs and makes monitoring simpler.

### D11. 2026-05-28 — Refusal classifier revision v1 → v2; rescore all raw outputs in place

**Decision:** Replace the v1 refusal classifier (14 narrow regex patterns) with a v2 expanded classifier covering all canonical refusal templates produced by modern instruction-tuned LLMs, including curly-apostrophe normalisation. Rescore all six existing HarmBench and XSTest `raw.jsonl` files in place (`scripts/rescore_harmbench.py`) — *do not re-run inference on TC1*. Re-run `make analyze` and `make report`. Document the revision openly in §6.1.1 of the FYP report and in this log.

**Rationale:** An external audit on 2026-05-28 identified that the v1 parser missed the most common modern refusal templates ("I can't fulfill this request", "I cannot provide", "I'm unable to assist", "I won't provide", "I don't condone", curly-apostrophe variants). Manual inspection of the v1 raw outputs confirmed the audit: clear safety refusals were being scored as harmful_compliance, inflating reported HarmBench ASR for all six runs. The v1 numbers would have remained as published findings in the FYP report unless corrected. Because the raw responses are saved on disk, rescoring is deterministic and does not require any new inference; rerunning on TC1 was therefore unnecessary and (under TC1's GPU-job policy) discouraged. The new classifier was validated by manual stratified audit of 55 sampled responses across the six runs; all sampled "newly classified as refusal" responses were unambiguous refusals, and all sampled "still flagged harmful" responses were genuine compliances or refuse-then-comply edge cases. Headline impact: Qwen 4B ΔASR flipped sign and acquired statistical significance (alignment_degradation under v2, vs alignment_improvement under v1); Qwen 1.7B ΔASR collapsed from −0.120 to −0.025 (still capability_collapse driven by the significant MMLU drop); Llama ΔASR moved from +0.030 to 0.000 (broad_degradation under v2, alignment_degradation under v1). Two of three labels changed. The framework itself — the capability-anchored interpretation procedure — is unchanged and continues to correctly diagnose the three pairs.

**Implementation:**
- `ethical_benchmark/benchmarks/utils.py`: replaced `DEFAULT_REFUSAL_PATTERNS` with ~40 comprehensive regexes; added `_normalise_for_refusal` (curly-apostrophe handling); added `match_refusal_pattern` (returns matched pattern for diagnostics).
- `scripts/rescore_harmbench.py` (new, ~280 lines): reads raw.jsonl, recomputes score_fields for HarmBench and XSTest using v2 classifier, rewrites summary.json. Emits redacted IDs-only diagnostic CSVs (`results/analysis/rescore_diagnostics_{harmbench,xstest}.csv`) and aggregate JSON (`results/analysis/rescore_aggregate.json`). Idempotent. No raw response content is ever printed or written to diagnostic outputs.
- `tests/test_refusal_parser.py`: added 36 regression tests (26 positive refusal templates, 6 negative controls, 3 curly-apostrophe variants, 1 diagnostic helper test). Total test suite: 126 → 162.
- `scripts/build_fyp_report.js`: added §6.1.1 (scorer revision history) and rewrote affected text throughout Chapter 6, Abstract, Ch10, Appendix D, Appendix G.

**Supersession note:** The in-place artifact handling described above was immediately superseded by D12 after Codex audit. Current repo state does **not** rely on rewritten raw outputs; it preserves `raw.jsonl`/`summary.json` and uses v2 sidecars.

### D12. 2026-05-27 — Preserve TC1 raw outputs; store v2 scoring as derived sidecars

**Decision:** Supersede the artifact-handling part of D11. Keep TC1-original `raw.jsonl` and `summary.json` immutable. Store corrected refusal scoring in derived `scores.v2.jsonl` files (prompt IDs + score_fields only; no prompt or response text) and `summary.v2.json` files. Update `compare_quant_pairs.py` to prefer complete v2 sidecars when present, while falling back to original files otherwise.

**Rationale:** Post-hoc scoring changes are methodology corrections, not new model generations. Preserving the original run files protects auditability and avoids contaminating the TC1 evidence trail. The v2 score sidecars are sufficient for aggregate metrics and paired bootstrap CIs without duplicating sensitive raw model outputs. The safe rescore script now regenerates sidecars, redacted diagnostics, and aggregate before/after counts while leaving all `raw.jsonl` and `summary.json` hashes unchanged.

### D14. 2026-06-06 — Judge classifier runs in full precision (fp16), not quantized

**Decision:** The HarmBench judge classifier (`cais/HarmBench-Llama-2-13b-cls`) runs in float16 (full precision) by default for the validation. The runner exposes `--precision {fp16,8bit,4bit}` defaulting to `fp16`; the sbatch requests fp16, probes and logs the actual GPU + VRAM at startup, and records the GPU/precision used in `summary.judge.harmbench_cls.json`. If the 13B classifier does not fit in fp16 on the available GPU (i.e. TC1's V100 is the 16 GB variant, ~26 GB needed for fp16), the documented fallback is `--precision 8bit` (~13–14 GB, far closer to full precision than the 4-bit NF4 used on the target models), reported explicitly. 4-bit is the last resort.

**Rationale:** The judge is the *reference instrument* used to validate the (4-bit-quantized) target models. Quantizing the judge itself with the same NF4 scheme would introduce exactly the confound the check exists to rule out — any judge–v2 disagreement could then be blamed on judge quantization rather than being informative about the target models. Full precision keeps the validation instrument clean. Logging the realised precision and hardware preserves reproducibility and makes any fallback transparent in the report (§6.12) rather than hidden. This reverses the original sbatch choice (NF4 "to fit the V100"), which optimised for fitting over fidelity; for a validation instrument, fidelity wins. Superseded the NF4 wording in §6.12 and the sbatch.

### D15. 2026-06-06 — Keep fp16 judge fidelity; reduce batch size before precision fallback

**Decision:** The TC1 judge sbatch keeps the HarmBench classifier in fp16 but lowers `--batch-size` from 8 to 4 and uses `low_cpu_mem_usage=True` when loading the local HF judge. If fp16 still OOMs on TC1, the first operational response is to reduce batch size further (2 or 1). Only after that should the job switch to the documented `--precision 8bit` fallback, and any fallback must be reported in the judge summary and §6.12.

**Rationale:** User's compute-node probe confirmed `Tesla V100-PCIE-32GB, 32768 MiB`, so the fp16 13B judge weights should fit in principle. The remaining memory risk is activation/KV-cache and loader overhead, not the card being a 16 GB variant. Reducing batch size preserves judge fidelity while giving fp16 more headroom; changing precision is a last-resort operational fallback, not the default scientific plan.

### D16. 2026-06-06 — Official HarmBench classifier supersedes the v2 regex for HarmBench ASR; refine alignment_degradation rule

**Decision:** The official HarmBench classifier (`cais/HarmBench-Llama-2-13b-cls`, fp16) is the **primary** scorer for HarmBench Attack Success Rate in all headline conclusions. The v2 refusal regex is demoted to a **secondary, refusal-based non-refusal-rate proxy**, retained in the repo and report for transparency. Scope is HarmBench-only: XSTest over-refusal stays v2-scored (the classifier does not judge over-refusal) and MMLU is unaffected. Separately, `classify_pair_change` is refined so `alignment_degradation` requires `harm_delta >= harm_tol AND capability_delta > -cap_tol` (capability preserved); ASR-up-with-capability-down now correctly falls through to `broad_degradation`.

**Rationale:** The judge validation (T20, job 61047, fp16 on a 32 GB V100, n=200×6, 0 parse errors) showed the v2 regex materially disagrees with the benchmark's own classifier — agreement is poor for Qwen (Cohen's κ ≈ 0.19–0.37) and high for Llama (κ ≈ 0.69–0.79). The regex equates "non-refusal" with "attack success" and therefore over-counts ASR, most severely for Qwen, which produces much non-refusal-but-not-harmful text. The disagreement is conclusion-level: under the judge the only statistically significant ΔASR moves from Qwen 4B (proxy: +0.065, CI [+0.025,+0.110]) to Qwen 1.7B (judge: +0.055, CI [+0.010,+0.100]), and the small-model direction flips from apparently-negative to significantly-positive. Keeping a scorer demonstrably over-counting ASR 3–4× on Qwen as the headline metric would be indefensible; the HarmBench paper specifies this classifier. The rule refinement enforces the report's own definition of alignment_degradation ("ASR up with capability preserved") — without it, Qwen 1.7B under the judge (ΔASR +0.055 significant, ΔMMLU −0.087 significant) would be mislabelled alignment_degradation rather than the honest broad_degradation. Verified the refinement changes no v2 pair labels.

**Impact (judge-primary, refined rule):** Qwen 1.7B → broad_degradation (significant ΔASR +0.055 and significant ΔMMLU −0.087 — the study's confirmed worst case); Qwen 4B → alignment_degradation but directional only (ΔASR +0.025, CI touches zero); Llama 3B → broad_degradation (ΔASR ≈ 0, significant ΔMMLU −0.043). Under the official classifier, NF4 never reduces true harmful compliance in any pair. The judge validation thus demonstrates the framework's diagnostic value by overturning a regex artefact and relocating the one robust safety regression to the smallest model. Implemented in `compare_quant_pairs.classify_pair_change`, `scripts/judge_agreement.py` (now emits judge bootstrap CIs + judge-primary labels), tests (`test_quant_analysis.py`, +2), and the FYP report (Tables 6.1/6.2/6.3, §6.1–§6.12, Abstract, Ch10).

### D13. 2026-05-27 — Judge-model scoring is a derived validation layer, not the primary artifact

**Decision:** Any LlamaGuard/API/HarmBench-classifier judge work must be implemented as a separate validation layer with its own sidecars, not as an overwrite of the v2 scorer or TC1-original outputs. Use a naming pattern such as `scores.judge.<judge>.jsonl` and `summary.judge.<judge>.json`. Judge diagnostics must be redacted and ID-based, just like the v2 rescore diagnostics. The current report remains v2-regex based unless a later decision explicitly promotes a judge scorer after validation.

**Rationale:** The v1→v2 incident showed that post-hoc scoring changes can materially alter conclusions. Treating judge-model scoring as an independent sensitivity check preserves the audit trail: raw generation outputs stay untouched, v2 regex results remain reproducible, and judge results can be compared side-by-side rather than silently replacing the current evidence. This also limits safety exposure: judge prompts may contain sensitive benchmark content internally, but logs, CSVs, and report snippets must contain only IDs, counts, labels, confidence/status fields, and redacted placeholders.

### D10. 2026-05-28 — Add alignment_improvement label to interpretation taxonomy

**Decision:** Extend `classify_pair_change` from four labels to five by adding `alignment_improvement`, which fires when `ΔASR ≤ −harm_tol AND |ΔOR| < refusal_tol AND ΔMMLU > −cap_tol`. The label is the symmetric mirror of `alignment_degradation` and is checked after the capability-collapse and alignment-degradation conditions but before `robust_preservation`.

**Rationale:** The original 4-label taxonomy was asymmetric on the safety axis: it had `alignment_degradation` for the bad direction (ASR up with capability preserved) but no mirror label for the good direction (ASR down with capability preserved). Qwen 4B (ΔASR=−0.045, ΔMMLU=−0.004, ΔOR=0.000) is the textbook case of a capability-preserving harmful-compliance reduction — a genuinely desirable outcome — but was falling through to the `broad_degradation` fallback, which inverts the scientific reading. Adding the symmetric label fixes Qwen 4B's classification without re-categorising Qwen 2B (still capability_collapse) or Llama (still alignment_degradation). The taxonomy is now symmetric around the safety axis: improvement and degradation are first-class outcomes, capability-collapse remains the sentinel for fake safety wins, and broad_degradation becomes a true fallback for mixed signals.

### D7. 2026-05-27 — Switch Qwen pairs from techwithsergiu to official Qwen3 models

**Decision:** Replace `techwithsergiu/Qwen3.5-text-2B` and `techwithsergiu/Qwen3.5-text-4B` with `Qwen/Qwen3-1.7B` and `Qwen/Qwen3-4B` respectively. Pair IDs, model aliases, and output directory paths remain unchanged.

**Rationale:** The `techwithsergiu` models are third-party uploads with a hybrid linear-attention/SSM architecture that requires `causal-conv1d` and `flash-linear-attention` as runtime dependencies. Without those libraries, the fallback PyTorch `conv1d` path raises `CUDNN_STATUS_NOT_INITIALIZED` on TC1's V100 during the very first inference call. Official Qwen3 models are standard GQA transformers with no extra library requirements, are widely tested, and are from the same Qwen family. Qwen3-1.7B (≈1.7 B) and Qwen3-4B (≈4 B) preserve the intended scale comparison. Additionally, our existing `enable_thinking=False` chat-template flag was written specifically for Qwen3's thinking mode, making these models an ideal fit for the pipeline.

| 2026-06-06 16:15 | `docs/PROJECT_LOG.md` | **Removed self-invalidating Git facts from the status snapshot (root-cause fix).** The §1 handoff block and TC1-access row had hard-coded the live push state ("origin/main is at `2914608`", "2 commits ahead", explicit unpushed-commit lists) — facts that go false the instant the next commit lands, which is what kept re-staling across the 15:45/16:00 sweeps. Replaced both with durable wording that defers to `git status -sb` / `git log --oneline origin/main..HEAD` and never asserts an ahead-count or hash. Exact commit hashes remain only in the §4 changelog rows, where they are historical (a record of what a past change did) and therefore safe. Convention going forward: the status snapshot describes durable state; volatile Git facts are looked up live, not written down. | Audit principle (correct): putting a moving Git fact in a current-state doc makes the fix commit immediately falsify it — "snake eating its own tail". The robust fix is to not record the count at all, not to bump it to the next number. | no | Claude |

Each of these has a single, well-defined purpose. They are stable references, edited only when their topic itself changes.

| `docs/archive/` | Superseded documents (kept for traceability, not authoritative). |

## 6. Maintenance contract (the rules that keep this repo coherent)

These are the standing conventions. They apply to every agent session (Claude, Codex, Cursor, Aider, or a human) and to every commit.

1. **Every change writes one row to the §4 changelog table.** Columns: `When (UTC+8) | Files | Change | Why / Notes | Report? | Who`. Timestamp is `YYYY-MM-DD HH:MM` local time. `Files` lists the actual paths touched. `Why / Notes` captures the rationale or the user request that triggered it. `Report?` is `yes` if `make report` was run, `no` if the change wasn't report-worthy. `Who` is the human author or the agent name (e.g., "Claude" or "Codex"). Append at the top.
2. **Every report-worthy change regenerates the FYP report** (`make report`) and bumps the `Report?` column to `yes`. A change is report-worthy if it touches methodology, system design, experimental setup, results, limitations / future work, or appendices. Edit `scripts/build_fyp_report_v5.js` (the canonical builder), never the docx. The docx has its own "Document Revision History" appendix that mirrors the report-affecting subset of this changelog.
3. **Update the §1 metadata table when you edit this file.** Bump `Last updated` to today's date and `Last updated by` to your name.
4. **Update §2 (open actions) when work appears or finishes.** Tick `[x]` when done and move the item (one line) into the new changelog row.
5. **Decisions go to §3, append-only.** A decision is a choice between alternatives with rationale. Never edit past decisions; if reversing one, append a new entry referencing the old.
6. **`AGENTS.md` and `CLAUDE.md` stay identical** (apart from the agent-name header). Edit both in the same commit. `diff AGENTS.md CLAUDE.md` should show only the header differences.
7. **No hand-edits to `.docx` files.** Generated docx files (FYP report) are artifacts; edit the source builder script.
8. **Never push or commit without a corresponding PROJECT_LOG.md entry.** Treat the log as part of the change, not a separate chore.
9. **Superseded files go to `docs/archive/`**, not the trash. Keep historical artifacts for traceability.

## 7. How to use this log

**When you (or a future Claude session) make a change to the repo:**
1. Update the relevant section here in the same change. Don't push code without a log entry.
2. If the change is just a file edit (typo, small refactor), add one line to the changelog.
3. If the change involves a real decision (choosing approach A over B, dropping scope, adopting a new convention), add an entry to §3 (Decisions) with the rationale.
4. If the change creates work for later, add to §2 (Open Actions).
5. If the change affects current state (e.g., experiments now running, environment broken, quota exhausted), update §1 (Status snapshot) in place.

**When you finish a task:**
1. Tick `[x]` next to the item in §2.
2. Move it (with a one-line note) into the latest changelog entry, or create a new dated changelog entry if it's substantial.

**When you make a decision:**
1. Append to §3 with date, decision, and rationale.
2. Never edit prior decisions. If reversing one, add a new entry that references the old.

**When in doubt, write it down here.** This file is the only thing that survives session resets, supervisor handovers, and your own forgetful future self.
